BARLEY â Futures were lower, partly in
sympathy with the decline In Wheat futures,
but mainly due to the discovery that the recent
drying winds have changed the character of
the grain this year. According to H. A.
Wright of the firm of Yates & Wright a good
deal of grain which would have been Brewing
was caught in the milk by the winds and
turned into Feed. This change will Increase
the quantity of Feed to about 65 or 70 per
cent of the crop and cut down the proportion [
of Brewing to correspond. This makes Feed
weak and would make Brewing strong if there
were any demand for It.
The cash market was fairly active at pre
vious prices.

Somers & Co. quote the Hay market as fol
lows In their circular:
"Total receipts of Hay for the week just
ended amount to 2100 tons, or 300 tons less than
for the week preceding. Although we are well
past the 1st of June, yet very little of the ar
rivals Is new crop Hay. Two or three cars
of new wheat have arrived, but as yet none of
them have been offered on the- market. Two
or three cars daily of new Volunteer have been
offered for sale, and. although an occasional
car shows up straight and clean, yet most
everything is mixed more or less with clover
and grass. The range at present Is from $7 to
$S per ton here.
"The old crop seems to hold out well, and
from all reports it would seem that there Is
enough to carry us well past the 1st of July.
The local demand I. very quiet, for most cus
tomers believe that by waiting they will be
able to stock up at considerably lower prires.
A careful Investigation shows that the Hay
crop is somewhat heavier than last year, and,
as we still have quite a supply of old Hay, it
Is very reasonable to believe that prices will
rule at considerably below last summer's range.
We do not expect extremely low prices, but
no one seems to be prepared to go out and pay
what they dM last season.
"It Is somewhat of a disappointment to
have to report that the Government order for
about 4000 tons, bids for which were received
on the 4th inst.. may not be left In San
Francisco. We have no assurance as to this,
but it Is unofficially stated that the north
will be favored with this order in spite of the
fact thaf' their prices were above ours.
"As to our local market we have to report
that the principal trade Js with the retailers,
and wn therefore find that the strictly gllt
edgc grades of Hay are selling fairly well."
A cargo of new Barley, Oat and Alfalfa Hay
came In and received a bid of $5 75 per ton,
but was not sold. . Â¦

The . feast of the sacred . heart of
Jesus "will be celebrated to-morrow at
St. Ignatius. -Church. - The devotion
was especially urged by the late Pope
Leo XIII shortly before his death.
There will be a solemn high mass
at. 9 a. m. and in the evening, a ser
mon and solemn benediction of the
blessed sacrament. Before the bene
diction.the solemn act of consecration
to the sacred heart will be recited by
the , entire congregation.. . After the
high mass in the morning and at 3:30
in the afternoon the children will be
dedicated to the' sacred.. heart." The
faithful have been preparing â¢ for this
feast by a novena or nine days' prayer.
Rev. .Henry Woods,' S.' J.,, has .been
conducting the novena and will con
clude it to-morrow^ night with an ap
propriate discourse.

DEVOUT SERVICES WILL
BE HELD AT ST. IGNATIUS
Carson City will be the scene of
carnival and jollity from July 2 until
July 7. The citizens of the Nevada
capital are making great preparations
for the entertainment of visitors and
expect that the attendance wijl be
larger than at any previous event of
a similar character ever held in the
State. John P. Meder, chairman of
the committee on publicity and pro
motion, is in this city and has already
secured many high-class attractions
and concessions. Mr. Meder says the
mountain town will outdo its effort of
three years ago and that the affair will
rival any on the coast.
Carson City Carnival.
Without seelng'lhe Diamond Palace would
be like visiting Europe without seeing Par
is. It 18 a leading feature of San Francis
co, and Is the most beautiful Jewelry
store in the world. Visitors or purchas
ers are equally welcome. 221 Montgom
ery, between Bush and Pine. â¢

Philip Eastwick Jr., cashier for the
International Banking Corporation,
testified as to the conversation at the
cashier's window when Jacob Eppin
ger was negotiating the loan with Col
onel Beck. He stated that the defend
ant wished to borrow $25,000 or $30,000.
Colonel Beck was willing to loan the
money, but asked 6 per cent Interest.
Eppinger said this was too high and a
compromise was finally made at 5%
per cent. Attorney Dunne subjected
the witness to a rigid cross-examina
tion, but was unable to shake his tes
timony.
The case will be resumed at 9:30 this
morning, when the cross-examination
of McFaul will be resumed.
W. C. Ledeme, receiving teller for the
London. Paris and American Bank,
testified as to having received the
check for $9800 issued by the Interna
tional Banking Corporation on April
14. He Identified the check and It was
admitted in evidence.
The defense then proceeded along the
line of the financing of the prosecution,
seeking to find now much money had
been raised to defray the expenses of
the trial, from what sources and in
what manner It .was expended.
Colonel Beck testified that the money
had been raised partially under his di
rection by a committee and had been
disbursed by him with the approval of
the committee. A portion of the mon
ey,- he said, was paid to J. C. Camp
bell to act as special prosecutor and
the remainder was turned over to
Wells, Fargo & Co. This money was
raised not only to prosecute Jacob Ep
pinger, but all persons who might be
connected with ' the failure. Attorney
Dunne attempted to learn from the
witness Just how much money had been
raised, but in line with a previous rul
ing Judge Liawlor sustained the pros
ecution's objection to the question.

Heney said there w,as no reason why
the affidavits should not be admitted
unless Oakland expected to win on
technicalities. Furthermore, it was im
possible to gather the data contained
in the affidavits in time. to furnish the
defendants a copy, but that copies
would be furnished by -this morning.
The matter was argued for over an
hour, but at thw finish Judge Gilbert
said he would allow the affidavits to be
admitted owing, to the serious nature
of the suit and the great questions in
volved. Attorney Heney proceeded
with the reading of. Adams' affidavit
and then offered additional ones from
George T. Lafiesche. William Alvord,
G. W. Kline. I. W.Hellman. George A.
Moore. Jacob Brith. P. McK. Duperu
and Henry S. Gore.
WHAT OAKIiAXD WANTS.
Garret W. McEnerney, who is asso
ciated with Heney and John Garber,
took exception to the statement made
by Mayor Olney regarding the under
standing about the. filing of affidavits.
He saia it had been understood that
the city of. Oakland through its attor
neys intended to file affidavits and as
the attorneys for plaintiffs could not
anticipate the nature of those docu
ments the affidavits offered by the
company could, not be served on the
defendants at the time the complaint
â¢was filed.
Olney claimed that the suit was
brought in reality to take away the
power of the city to regulate water
rates and that the company simply
wanted to put ' the affidavits into the
case to strengthen Its position.
Heney replied, saying the sole ques
tion before the court was not whether
the plaintiff had established a case,
but whether a temporary Injunction
should be granted to prevent the de
fendants from putting arbitrary, rates
Into effect. The admission of supple
mentary affidavits would simply pro
vide additional Information to aid the
court to determine the question of de
nying or granting the injunction
prayed for. Under the law the rates
should have been fixed in February,
but they were not fixed until May 31
and then arbitrarily. The affidavits
would -'show -those 'facts and should be
admitted. -â¢.'- r- â¢'.â¢'-â¢
Attorney Francis J. Heney opened
the case for the company by explaining
to the court the nature of the action.
His contention was that the rates the
city proposes to put into effect on July
1 will not give the company more than
6 per cent on its Investment and that
amount would leave the company in
debt to the amount of 510,000 at the end
of each year the rates are In" effect.
The actu U value of the plant, accord-
Ing to the company's figures, is $7,500,
000. and the additional value of the
franchise Is $1,000,000. The com
pany has a bonded Indebtedness of
$3." n 0,000. upon which It has to pay In
terest at the rate of 5 per cent i.er
annum, but this will be an impossibil
ity if the rates fixed by. the Council
are allowed to stand.
In order to establish his contention
Attorney Heney offered an affidavit
signed by Arthur L. Adams, an expert
engineer, and former manager of the
company. Heney started to read the
document, but Mayor Warren Olney of
Oakland, who is the leading counsel
for the city, objected that under the
rules of the court affidavits were not
admissible. He argued that the case
before the court was one Involving
the rights of every municipality in the
State and that unless the court up
held its time-honored rule the rights
of all legislative bodies would be in
Jeopardy.
RIGHTS INVOLVED.
The legal battle between the Contra
Coeta Water Company and the city of
Oakland began yesterday before Unit
ed States Circuit Judge Gilbert and
gives promise of being a long fight.
The company asks for an injunction to
restrain the city from putting into ef
fect on July 1 the rates established by
the City Council May 31. Under the
contract w,ith the company the. city
sets the rates to be collected from con
sumers of water and in fixing those
rates the valuation of the plant is
taken as a basis. The Council set the
valuation this year. at $4,700,000. but
the company contends their plant is
worth JR. 500. 000. The company wants
that amount taken as the basis for
fixing the rates, hence the application
for an injunction.
When the case was called the com
pany secured an order from the court
to compel the defendant to furnish to
the plaintiff all the data that was used
to arrive at the rates fixed by ' the
Council in May. In the afternoon it
gained another point by securing the
admission of affidavits supplementary
to the bill of complaint.

An attempt was made t r obtain from
the witness a statement regarding the
amount of money paid Mr. Campbell as
special prosecutor, in order to show
animus of the witness. The jury was
dismissed and the question argued at
length. The prosecution contended
that the mere fact that a special prose
cutor was employed was sufficient evi
dence of the Interest of the witness in
the case and that the sum of money
paid him for his services was In no
sense a point for the Jury to consider,
but rather a private business trans-
At the opening of the morning ses
elon, Colonel. Beck, manager of the In
ternational Banking Corporation, re
sumed the stand. He testified as to
the number of: years he had been In
the banking business and as to his
business relations with the firm of Ep
pinger & Co. On cross-examination by
Attorney Ach the witness stated that
he had solicited business from the Ep
pingers, as he thought they would be
good customers. He had made them
one loan prior to that made In April
and the amount had been paid. Dur
ing the course of the examination At
torney Ach was rebuked by the court
for the manner in which he was con
ducting the examination. He ex
plained that there was no intent to
take up the time of the court and the
purport of his questions would develop
later.
ATTORNEY IS REBUKED.
The prosecution in the case of Jacob
Eppinger, charged with obtaining
money on worthless warehouse receipts,
dug into the meat of the case late yes
terday afternoon when the work of
tracing the. course of the receipts and
the disposition of the grain was begun.
W. B. Cutter of the firm of Cutter &
Moseley testified *that he had on De
cember 2, 1902," purchased warehouse
receipts Nos. 706, 707, 708 and 709 from
M. Blum & Co. -n December 4 he sent
these receipts to Eppinger & Co. with
the following letter:
Enclosed find warehouse receipts covering
lots 700. 707. 708 and 709. which please tele
phone to Port Costa to deliver on the French
bark Pierre Lotl. Your immediate attention
will oblige, as we would like to get started
early this morning so as to get finished. Ke
spectfully, CUTTER & MOSEL.EY.
Two of the lots mentioned are those
which the indictment charges Jacob
Eppinger with having borrowed upon
in April of 1903. In order to follow up
the transaction, Hugh McFaul, a
weigher employed In the warehouse at
Crockett, testified that he had weighed
the grain mentioned In the hypothecat
ed receipts and seen it loaded on the
bark Pierre Loti during the month of
December, 1902.* He also jaw the ves
sel sail away with the grain in her
hold. .vV Â¦Â¦*.Â¦.;?â¢'â¢â¢Â¦. . : - 'Â¦Â¦'-:
The board approved the map of Â¦ the
assessment district for changes of
grades on Greenwich street, between
Hyde and Larkin.
City Engineer Woodward reported
that the cost of grading all cross
streets between Twenty-sixth and
Army streets, from Alabama street to
San Bruno road, Is far in excess of
one-half of the assessed value of prop
erty liable therefor and that the work
cannot be done und$r public contract.
The Civil Service Commission sent a
request that general information be
furnished by the board regarding the
qualifications of civil service eligibles
for street sweepers, with a view to hold-
Ing an examination therefor. * The
Merchants' Association asked that the
present sweepers have an equal chance
In the preparation of the eligible list.
The commission also asked to be ad
vised how many superintendents,
assistant superintendents, inspectors
and foremen will be needed for the
municipal street cleaning plant. Presi
dent Schmitz was authorized to confer
with the commission.
M. L. Schmitt ug/ped that a uniform
width for brick walls in buildings.be
adopted. Schmitt wanted the width
fixed at thirteen inches, which, he said.
was acceptable to the Fire Depart
ment^ He was instructed to file a peti
tion on the subject, so that the build-
Ing ordinance may be amended by the
Supervisors.
The board approved the specifica
tions for water works for the new
pesthouse and asked the Supervisors
for authority to enter into a contract
therefor.
City Engineer Woodward reported
that Thirty-second avenue South, from
d street to the water, line,' about 350
feet, is private property and that a
fence thereon is not an obstruction.
Contracts were awarded yesterday
by the Board of Public Works to
Frank McSheehy for additions to the
Dudley Stone School building at $12,
492, and for additions to the Lowell
High School building at $2240.
Bids were opened for making cer
tain additions to the Richmond School
building. Fred C. Jones' bid was $21,
450 and- the Deneen Building Com
pany's $18,000. The contract will be
awarded to the latter after the Board
of Education has passed on the mat
ter.
